<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Architecture_of_Spaun.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1280" data-file-width="1259" decoding="async" height="315" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Architecture_of_Spaun.jpeg/310px-Architecture_of_Spaun.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Architecture_of_Spaun.jpeg/465px-Architecture_of_Spaun.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Architecture_of_Spaun.jpeg/620px-Architecture_of_Spaun.jpeg 2x" width="310"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Architecture_of_Spaun.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Simplified diagram of <i>Spaun</i>, a 2.5-million-neuron computational model of the brain. <b>(A)</b> The corresponding physical regions and connections of the human brain. <b>(B)</b> The mental architecture of Spaun.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Spaun_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-Spaun-117">[117]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Neuroscience">Neuroscience</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mind&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Neuroscience">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Cognitive_neuroscience" title="Cognitive neuroscience">Cognitive neuroscience</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thought_identification" title="Thought identification">Thought identification</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Epigenetics_in_learning_and_memory" title="Epigenetics in learning and memory">Epigenetics in learning and memory</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Neuroscience" title="Neuroscience">Neuroscience</a> studies the <a href="/wiki/Nervous_system" title="Nervous system">nervous system</a>, the physical basis of the mind. At the systems level, neuroscientists investigate how <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biological_neural_networks" title="Biological neural networks">biological neural networks</a> form and physiologically interact to produce mental functions and content such as <a href="/wiki/Reflex" title="Reflex">reflexes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Multisensory_integration" title="Multisensory integration">multisensory integration</a>, <a href="/wiki/Motor_coordination" title="Motor coordination">motor coordination</a>, <a href="/wiki/Circadian_rhythm" title="Circadian rhythm">circadian rhythms</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emotion" title="Emotion">emotional responses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Learning" title="Learning">learning</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Memory" title="Memory">memory</a>.  The underlying physical basis of <a href="/wiki/Learning" title="Learning">learning</a> and <a href="/wiki/Memory" title="Memory">memory</a> is likely dynamic changes in <a href="/wiki/Gene_expression" title="Gene expression">gene expression</a> that occur in <a href="/wiki/Brain" title="Brain">brain</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neurons" title="Neurons">neurons</a>.  Such expression changes are introduced by <a href="/wiki/Epigenetics" title="Epigenetics">epigenetic</a> mechanisms.  <a href="/wiki/Epigenetics" title="Epigenetics">Epigenetic</a> regulation of gene expression ordinarily involves chemical modification of <a href="/wiki/DNA" title="DNA">DNA</a> or DNA-associated <a href="/wiki/Histone" title="Histone">histone</a> proteins.  Such chemical modifications can cause long-lasting changes in gene expression.  Epigenetic mechanisms employed in learning and memory include the <a href="/wiki/DNA_(cytosine-5)-methyltransferase_3A" title="DNA (cytosine-5)-methyltransferase 3A">DNMT3A</a> promoted <a href="/wiki/DNA_methylation" title="DNA methylation">methylation</a> and <a href="/wiki/TET_enzymes" title="TET enzymes">TET</a> promoted <a href="/wiki/DNA_demethylation" title="DNA demethylation">demethylation</a> of <a href="/wiki/Neuron" title="Neuron">neuronal</a> DNA as well as <a href="/wiki/Histone_methylation" title="Histone methylation">methylation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Histone_acetylation_and_deacetylation" title="Histone acetylation and deacetylation">acetylation and deacetylation</a> of neuronal histone proteins. Also, long term excitation of <a href="/wiki/Neural_pathway" title="Neural pathway">neural pathways</a> and subsequent endocrinal signaling, can provide a capacity for structural activation of <a href="/wiki/Gene_expression" title="Gene expression">gene expression</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Histone_code" title="Histone code">histone code</a>; allowing a potential mechanism of throughput epigenetic interaction with the <a href="/wiki/Nervous_system" title="Nervous system">nervous system</a>.
</p><p>At a larger scale, efforts in <a href="/wiki/Computational_neuroscience" title="Computational neuroscience">computational neuroscience</a> have developed large-scale models that simulate simple, functioning brains.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Spaun_117-1"><a href="#cite_note-Spaun-117">[117]</a></sup> As of 2012, such models include the <a href="/wiki/Thalamus" title="Thalamus">thalamus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basal_ganglia" title="Basal ganglia">basal ganglia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prefrontal_cortex" title="Prefrontal cortex">prefrontal cortex</a>, <a href="/wiki/Motor_cortex" title="Motor cortex">motor cortex</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Occipital_cortex" title="Occipital cortex">occipital cortex</a>, and consequentially simulated brains can learn, respond to visual stimuli, coordinate motor responses, form short-term memories, and learn to respond to patterns. Currently, researchers aim to program the <a href="/wiki/Hippocampus" title="Hippocampus">hippocampus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Limbic_system" title="Limbic system">limbic system</a>, hypothetically imbuing the simulated mind with <a href="/wiki/Long-term_memory" title="Long-term memory">long-term memory</a> and crude <a href="/wiki/Emotion" title="Emotion">emotions</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNRG_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-CNRG-118">[118]</a></sup>
</p><p>By contrast, <a href="/wiki/Affective_neuroscience" title="Affective neuroscience">affective neuroscience</a> studies the neural mechanisms of <a href="/wiki/Personality_psychology" title="Personality psychology">personality</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emotion" title="Emotion">emotion</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mood_(psychology)" title="Mood (psychology)">mood</a> primarily through experimental tasks.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cognitive_science">Cognitive science</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mind&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Cognitive science">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-Expand_section plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg"><img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="20"/></a></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs expansion</b>. You can help by <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Mind&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.  <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">May 2013</span>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cognitive_science" title="Cognitive science">Cognitive science</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Cognitive_science" title="Cognitive science">Cognitive science</a> examines the mental functions that give rise to <a href="/wiki/Information_processing" title="Information processing">information processing</a>, termed <a href="/wiki/Cognition" title="Cognition">cognition</a>. These include <a href="/wiki/Perception" title="Perception">perception</a>, <a href="/wiki/Attention" title="Attention">attention</a>, <a href="/wiki/Working_memory" title="Working memory">working memory</a>, <a href="/wiki/Long-term_memory" title="Long-term memory">long-term memory</a>, producing and understanding <a href="/wiki/Language" title="Language">language</a>, <a href="/wiki/Learning" title="Learning">learning</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reason" title="Reason">reasoning</a>, <a href="/wiki/Problem_solving" title="Problem solving">problem solving</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Decision_making" title="Decision making">decision making</a>. Cognitive science seeks to understand thinking "in terms of representational structures in the mind and computational procedures that operate on those structures".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stanford1_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-stanford1-119">[119]</a></sup>
</p><p>At the birth of cognitive science in the 1960s and 1970s, the paradigm of the <a href="/wiki/Computational_theory_of_mind" title="Computational theory of mind">computational theory of mind</a> was widely adopted. This paradigm holds that the mind is essentially a computational system, and its explanation needs to be provided in terms of a <a href="/wiki/Computation" title="Computation"><i>computational description</i></a>. More recently, rival paradigms gained ground within cognitive science, namely the <a href="/wiki/Cognitive_neuroscience" title="Cognitive neuroscience"><i>neurophysical description</i></a> and the <a href="/wiki/Intentionality" title="Intentionality"><i>intentional description</i></a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup>
</p><p>Though the interface between <a href="/wiki/Neuroscience" title="Neuroscience">neuroscience</a> and an exact model of <a href="/wiki/Cognition" title="Cognition">cognition</a> is not yet made, progress in <a href="/wiki/Biological_neuron_model" title="Biological neuron model">biological neuron models</a> help to mathematically quantify <a href="/wiki/Cognitive_neuroscience" title="Cognitive neuroscience">cognitive neuroscience</a>; and elaborate a theory of mind that can be provable. However a theoretically fundamental synthesis in psychology, cognitive science, neuroscience, and <a href="/wiki/Biophysics" title="Biophysics">biophysics</a> must be made; for the problem of mind and its faculties to gain tractable scientific ground. 
</p><p>Over the past years, research in cognitive sciences has highlighted the importance of the body for cognition. Proponents of the <a href="/wiki/Embodied_cognition" title="Embodied cognition">embodied cognition theory</a> of mind hold that cognition (and mental phenomena) is the product of active interactions between individuals and their surrounding environment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Psychology">Psychology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mind&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Psychology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Neuropsychology" title="Neuropsychology">Neuropsychology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Psyche_(psychology)" title="Psyche (psychology)">Psyche</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Unconscious_mind" title="Unconscious mind">Unconscious mind</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Psychology" title="Psychology">Psychology</a> is the scientific study of human behavior, mental functioning, and experience. As both an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academic_field" title="Academic field">academic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Applied_science" title="Applied science">applied</a> discipline, Psychology involves the <a href="/wiki/Science" title="Science">scientific study</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mental_process" title="Mental process">mental processes</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Perception" title="Perception">perception</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cognition" title="Cognition">cognition</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emotion" title="Emotion">emotion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Personality_psychology" title="Personality psychology">personality</a>, as well as environmental influences, such as social and cultural influences, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interpersonal_relationships" title="Interpersonal relationships">interpersonal relationships</a>, in order to devise theories of human behavior. Psychological patterns can be understood as low cost ways of information processing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup>  Psychology also refers to the application of such <a href="/wiki/Knowledge" title="Knowledge">knowledge</a> to various spheres of <a href="/wiki/Human_behavior" title="Human behavior">human activity</a>, including problems of individuals' <a href="/wiki/Everyday_life" title="Everyday life">daily lives</a> and the treatment of <a href="/wiki/Mental_health" title="Mental health">mental health</a> problems.
</p><p>Psychology differs from the other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_sciences" title="Social sciences">social sciences</a> (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Anthropology" title="Anthropology">anthropology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economics" title="Economics">economics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Political_science" title="Political science">political science</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sociology" title="Sociology">sociology</a>) due to its focus on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Experimentation" title="Experimentation">experimentation</a> at the scale of the individual, or individuals in small groups as opposed to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Group_(sociology)" title="Group (sociology)">large groups</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Institutions" title="Institutions">institutions</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Societies" title="Societies">societies</a>. Historically, psychology differed from <a href="/wiki/Biology" title="Biology">biology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Neuroscience" title="Neuroscience">neuroscience</a> in that it was primarily concerned with mind rather than brain. Modern psychological science incorporates <a href="/wiki/Psychophysiology" title="Psychophysiology">physiological</a> and <a href="/wiki/Neuropsychology" title="Neuropsychology">neurological</a> processes into its conceptions of <a href="/wiki/Perception" title="Perception">perception</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cognition" title="Cognition">cognition</a>, behaviour, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mental_disorders" title="Mental disorders">mental disorders</a>.
</p>
<h3><span id="Psychiatry.2C_Neurology_and_Neurosurgery"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Psychiatry,_Neurology_and_Neurosurgery">Psychiatry, Neurology and Neurosurgery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mind&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Psychiatry, Neurology and Neurosurgery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Psychiatry" title="Psychiatry">Psychiatry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neurology" title="Neurology">Neurology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Neurosurgery" title="Neurosurgery">Neurosurgery</a> are the specialties within the field of Medicine that are devoted to the study of the mind and to the treatment of humans with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mental_disorders" title="Mental disorders">mental disorders</a> and other medical conditions affecting the mind and nervous system. Psychiatrists, Neurologists and Neurosurgeons conduct research in clinical, academic and industry settings.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Mental_health">Mental health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mind&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Mental health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mental_health" title="Mental health">Mental health</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-More_citations_needed plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Mind&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br/><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Mind%22" rel="nofollow">"Mind"</a> – <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22Mind%22+-wikipedia&amp;tbs=ar:1" rel="nofollow">news</a> <b>·</b> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Mind%22&amp;tbs=bkt:s&amp;tbm=bks" rel="nofollow">newspapers</a> <b>·</b> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Mind%22+-wikipedia" rel="nofollow">books</a> <b>·</b> <a class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Mind%22" rel="nofollow">scholar</a> <b>·</b> <a class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Mind%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on" rel="nofollow">JSTOR</a></span></small></span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">December 2021</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>By analogy with the health of the body, one can speak metaphorically of a state of health of the mind, or <a href="/wiki/Mental_health" title="Mental health">mental health</a>. <a href="/wiki/Merriam-Webster" title="Merriam-Webster">Merriam-Webster</a> defines mental health as "a state of emotional and psychological well-being in which an individual is able to use his or her cognitive and emotional capabilities, function in society, and meet the ordinary demands of everyday life". According to the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> (WHO), there is no one "official" definition of mental health. Cultural differences, subjective assessments, and competing professional theories all affect how "mental health" is defined. In general, most experts agree that "mental health" and "<a href="/wiki/Mental_disorder" title="Mental disorder">mental disorder</a>" are not opposites. In other words, the absence of a recognized mental disorder is not necessarily an indicator of mental health.
</p><p>One way to think about mental health is by looking at how effectively and successfully a person functions. Feeling capable and competent; being able to handle normal levels of stress, maintaining satisfying relationships, and leading an independent life; and being able to "bounce back" or recover from difficult situations, are all signs of mental health.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Psychotherapy" title="Psychotherapy">Psychotherapy</a> is an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interpersonal" title="Interpersonal">interpersonal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Interpersonal_relationship" title="Interpersonal relationship">relational</a> intervention used by trained psychotherapists to aid <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Client" title="wikt:Client">clients</a> in problems of living. This usually includes increasing individual sense of <a href="/wiki/Well-being" title="Well-being">well-being</a> and reducing subjective discomforting experience. Psychotherapists employ a range of techniques based on experiential relationship building, <a href="/wiki/Dialogue" title="Dialogue">dialogue</a>, <a href="/wiki/Communication" title="Communication">communication</a> and <a href="/wiki/Behavior" title="Behavior">behavior</a> change and that are designed to improve the <a href="/wiki/Mental_health" title="Mental health">mental health</a> of a client or patient, or to improve group relationships (such as in a <a href="/wiki/Family" title="Family">family</a>). Most forms of psychotherapy use only spoken <a href="/wiki/Conversation" title="Conversation">conversation</a>, though some also use various other forms of communication such as the written word, <a href="/wiki/Art" title="Art">art</a>, <a href="/wiki/Drama" title="Drama">drama</a>, <a href="/wiki/Narrative" title="Narrative">narrative</a> story, or therapeutic touch. Psychotherapy occurs within a structured encounter between a trained <a href="/wiki/Therapist" title="Therapist">therapist</a> and client(s). Purposeful, theoretically based psychotherapy began in the 19th century with <a href="/wiki/Psychoanalysis" title="Psychoanalysis">psychoanalysis</a>; since then, scores of other approaches have been developed and continue to be created.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Non-human">Non-human</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mind&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Non-human">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-More_citations_needed plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Mind&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br/><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Mind%22" rel="nofollow">"Mind"</a> – <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22Mind%22+-wikipedia&amp;tbs=ar:1" rel="nofollow">news</a> <b>·</b> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Mind%22&amp;tbs=bkt:s&amp;tbm=bks" rel="nofollow">newspapers</a> <b>·</b> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Mind%22+-wikipedia" rel="nofollow">books</a> <b>·</b> <a class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Mind%22" rel="nofollow">scholar</a> <b>·</b> <a class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Mind%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on" rel="nofollow">JSTOR</a></span></small></span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">December 2021</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Animal_cognition">Animal cognition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mind&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Animal cognition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Animal_cognition" title="Animal cognition">Animal cognition</a>, or cognitive ethology, is the title given to a modern approach to the mental capacities of animals. It has developed out of <a href="/wiki/Comparative_psychology" title="Comparative psychology">comparative psychology</a>, but has also been strongly influenced by the approach of <a href="/wiki/Ethology" title="Ethology">ethology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Behavioral_ecology" title="Behavioral ecology">behavioral ecology</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Evolutionary_psychology" title="Evolutionary psychology">evolutionary psychology</a>. Much of what used to be considered under the title of "animal intelligence" is now thought of under this heading. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Animal_language_acquisition" title="Animal language acquisition">Animal language acquisition</a>, attempting to discern or understand the degree to which animal cognition can be revealed by <a href="/wiki/Linguistics" title="Linguistics">linguistics</a>-related study, has been controversial among <a href="/wiki/Cognitive_linguistics" title="Cognitive linguistics">cognitive linguists</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Artificial_intelligence">Artificial intelligence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mind&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Artificial intelligence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Philosophy_of_artificial_intelligence" title="Philosophy of artificial intelligence">Philosophy of artificial intelligence</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Forest_of_synthetic_pyramidal_dendrites_grown_using_Cajal%27s_laws_of_neuronal_branching.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="650" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Forest_of_synthetic_pyramidal_dendrites_grown_using_Cajal%27s_laws_of_neuronal_branching.png/220px-Forest_of_synthetic_pyramidal_dendrites_grown_using_Cajal%27s_laws_of_neuronal_branching.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Forest_of_synthetic_pyramidal_dendrites_grown_using_Cajal%27s_laws_of_neuronal_branching.png/330px-Forest_of_synthetic_pyramidal_dendrites_grown_using_Cajal%27s_laws_of_neuronal_branching.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Forest_of_synthetic_pyramidal_dendrites_grown_using_Cajal%27s_laws_of_neuronal_branching.png/440px-Forest_of_synthetic_pyramidal_dendrites_grown_using_Cajal%27s_laws_of_neuronal_branching.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Forest_of_synthetic_pyramidal_dendrites_grown_using_Cajal%27s_laws_of_neuronal_branching.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Computer_simulation" title="Computer simulation">Computer simulation</a> of the branching architecture of the <a href="/wiki/Dendrite" title="Dendrite">dendrites</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pyramidal_neuron" title="Pyramidal neuron">pyramidal neurons</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup></div></div></div><p> In 1950 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alan_M._Turing" title="Alan M. Turing">Alan M. Turing</a> published "Computing machinery and intelligence" in <i><a href="/wiki/Mind_(journal)" title="Mind (journal)">Mind</a></i>, in which he proposed that machines could be tested for intelligence using questions and answers. This process is now named the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turing_Test" title="Turing Test">Turing Test</a>. The term <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Artificial_Intelligence" title="Artificial Intelligence">Artificial Intelligence</a> (AI) was first used by <a href="/wiki/John_McCarthy_(computer_scientist)" title="John McCarthy (computer scientist)">John McCarthy</a> who considered it to mean "the science and engineering of making intelligent machines".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> It can also refer to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intelligence_(trait)" title="Intelligence (trait)">intelligence</a> as exhibited by an artificial (<i>man-made</i>, <i>non-natural</i>, <i>manufactured</i>) entity. AI is studied in overlapping fields of <a href="/wiki/Computer_science" title="Computer science">computer science</a>, <a href="/wiki/Psychology" title="Psychology">psychology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neuroscience" title="Neuroscience">neuroscience</a> and <a href="/wiki/Engineering" title="Engineering">engineering</a>, dealing with intelligent <a href="/wiki/Behavior" title="Behavior">behavior</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Learn" title="Learn">learning</a> and <a href="/wiki/Adaptation" title="Adaptation">adaptation</a> and usually developed using customized <a href="/wiki/Machine" title="Machine">machines</a> or <a href="/wiki/Computer" title="Computer">computers</a>.
</p><p>Research in AI is concerned with producing machines to automate tasks requiring intelligent behavior. Examples include <a href="/wiki/Control_system" title="Control system">control</a>, <a href="/wiki/Automated_planning_and_scheduling" title="Automated planning and scheduling">planning and scheduling</a>, the ability to answer diagnostic and consumer questions, <a href="/wiki/Handwriting_recognition" title="Handwriting recognition">handwriting</a>, <a href="/wiki/Natural_language" title="Natural language">natural language</a>, <a href="/wiki/Speech_recognition" title="Speech recognition">speech</a> and <a href="/wiki/Facial_recognition_system" title="Facial recognition system">facial recognition</a>. As such, the study of AI has also become an engineering discipline, focused on providing solutions to real life problems, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Knowledge_mining" title="Knowledge mining">knowledge mining</a>, <a href="/wiki/Software" title="Software">software</a> applications, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Strategy_games" title="Strategy games">strategy games</a> like <a href="/wiki/Computer_chess" title="Computer chess">computer chess</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Video_game" title="Video game">video games</a>. One of the biggest limitations of AI is in the domain of actual machine comprehension. Consequentially <a href="/wiki/Natural-language_understanding" title="Natural-language understanding">natural-language understanding</a> and <a href="/wiki/Connectionism" title="Connectionism">connectionism</a> (where behavior of neural networks is investigated) are areas of active research and development.
</p><p>The debate about the nature of the mind is relevant to the development of <a href="/wiki/Artificial_intelligence" title="Artificial intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>. If the mind is indeed a thing separate from or higher than the functioning of the brain, then hypothetically it would be much more difficult to recreate within a machine, if it were possible at all. If, on the other hand, the mind is no more than the aggregated functions of the brain, then it will be possible to create a machine with a recognisable mind (though possibly only with computers much different from today's), by simple virtue of the fact that such a machine already exists in the form of the human brain.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mind&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-More_citations_needed plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Mind&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br/><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Mind%22" rel="nofollow">"Mind"</a> – <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22Mind%22+-wikipedia&amp;tbs=ar:1" rel="nofollow">news</a> <b>·</b> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Mind%22&amp;tbs=bkt:s&amp;tbm=bks" rel="nofollow">newspapers</a> <b>·</b> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Mind%22+-wikipedia" rel="nofollow">books</a> <b>·</b> <a class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Mind%22" rel="nofollow">scholar</a> <b>·</b> <a class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Mind%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on" rel="nofollow">JSTOR</a></span></small></span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">December 2021</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Many religions associate spiritual qualities to the human mind. These are often tightly connected to their <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mythology" title="Mythology">mythology</a> and ideas of <a href="/wiki/Afterlife" title="Afterlife">afterlife</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">Indian</a> <a href="/wiki/Philosopher" title="Philosopher">philosopher</a>-sage <a href="/wiki/Sri_Aurobindo" title="Sri Aurobindo">Sri Aurobindo</a> attempted to unite the Eastern and Western psychological traditions with his <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Integral_psychology_(Sri_Aurobindo)" title="Integral psychology (Sri Aurobindo)">integral psychology</a>, as have many philosophers and <a href="/wiki/New_religious_movement" title="New religious movement">New religious movements</a>. <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a> teaches that "moach shalit al halev", the mind rules the heart; humans can approach the Divine intellectually, through learning and behaving according to the Divine Will as enclothed in the Torah, and use that deep logical understanding to elicit and guide emotional arousal during prayer. <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> has tended to see the mind (Greek <i><a href="/wiki/Nous" title="Nous">nous</a></i>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> as distinct from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soul_(spirit)" title="Soul (spirit)">soul</a> (Greek <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Psuche" title="Psuche">psuche</a></i>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> and sometimes further distinguished the <a href="/wiki/Vitalism" title="Vitalism">spirit</a> (Greek <i><a href="/wiki/Pneuma" title="Pneuma">pneuma</a></i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Esotericism" title="Esotericism">Western esoteric traditions</a> sometimes refer to a <a href="/wiki/Mental_body" title="Mental body">mental body</a> that exists on a plane other than the physical. <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a>'s various philosophical schools have debated whether the human <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soul_(spirit)" title="Soul (spirit)">soul</a> (Sanskrit <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atman_(Hinduism)" title="Atman (Hinduism)">atman</a></i>) is distinct from, or identical to, <i><a href="/wiki/Brahman" title="Brahman">Brahman</a></i>, the <a href="/wiki/Divinity" title="Divinity">divine</a> <a href="/wiki/Reality" title="Reality">reality</a>. <a href="/wiki/Taoism" title="Taoism">Taoism</a> sees the human being as contiguous with natural forces, and the mind as not separate from the <a href="/wiki/Human_body" title="Human body">body</a>. <a href="/wiki/Confucianism" title="Confucianism">Confucianism</a> sees the mind, like the body, as inherently perfectible.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Buddhism"><a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mind&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Buddhism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Buddhism_and_psychology" title="Buddhism and psychology">Buddhism and psychology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vij%C3%B1%C4%81na" title="Vijñāna">Vijñāna</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C5%9A%C5%ABnyat%C4%81" title="Śūnyatā">Śūnyatā</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shentong" title="Shentong">Shentong</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rangtong" title="Rangtong">Rangtong</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yogacara" title="Yogacara">Yogacara</a></div>
<p>Buddhist teachings explain the moment-to-moment manifestation of the mind-stream.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Karunamuni2017_9-2"><a href="#cite_note-Karunamuni2017-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aggregates_10-2"><a href="#cite_note-Aggregates-10">[10]</a></sup> The components that make up the mind are known as the five aggregates (i.e., material form, feelings, perception, volition, and sensory consciousness), which arise and pass away continuously. The arising and passing of these aggregates in the present moment is described as being influenced by five causal laws: biological laws, psychological laws, physical laws, volitional laws, and universal laws.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aggregates_10-3"><a href="#cite_note-Aggregates-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Karunamuni2017_9-3"><a href="#cite_note-Karunamuni2017-9">[9]</a></sup> The Buddhist practice of <a href="/wiki/Mindfulness" title="Mindfulness">mindfulness</a> involves attending to this constantly changing mind-stream.
</p><p>According to <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhist</a> philosopher <a href="/wiki/Dharmakirti" title="Dharmakirti">Dharmakirti</a>, the mind has two fundamental qualities: "clarity and cognizes". If something is not those two qualities, it cannot validly be called mind. "Clarity" refers to the fact that mind has no color, shape, size, location, weight, or any other physical characteristic, and "cognizes" that it functions to know or perceive objects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> "Knowing" refers to the fact that mind is aware of the contents of experience, and that, in order to exist, mind must be cognizing an object. You cannot have a mind – whose function is to cognize an object – existing without cognizing an object.
</p><p>Mind, in Buddhism, is also described as being "space-like" and "illusion-like". Mind is space-like in the sense that it is not physically obstructive. It has no qualities which would prevent it from existing. In <a href="/wiki/Mahayana" title="Mahayana">Mahayana</a> Buddhism, mind is illusion-like in the sense that it is empty of inherent existence. This does not mean it does not exist, it means that it exists in a manner that is counter to our ordinary way of misperceiving how phenomena exist, according to Buddhism. When the mind is itself cognized properly, without misperceiving its mode of existence, it appears to exist like an illusion. There is a big difference however between being "space and illusion" and being "space-like" and "illusion-like". Mind is not composed of space, it just shares some descriptive similarities to space. Mind is not an illusion, it just shares some descriptive qualities with illusions.
</p><p>Buddhism posits that there is no inherent, unchanging identity (Inherent I, Inherent Me) or phenomena (Ultimate self, inherent self, Atman, Soul, Self-essence, Jiva, Ishvara, humanness essence, etc.) which is the experiencer of our experiences and the agent of our actions. In other words, human beings consist of merely a body and a mind, and nothing extra. Within the body there is no part or set of parts which is – by itself or themselves – the person. Similarly, within the mind there is no part or set of parts which are themselves "the person". A human being merely consists of five aggregates, or <i><a href="/wiki/Skandha" title="Skandha">skandhas</a></i> and nothing else.
</p><p>In the same way, "mind" is what can be validly conceptually labelled onto our mere experience of clarity and knowing. There is something separate and apart from clarity and knowing which is "Awareness", in Buddhism. "Mind" is that part of experience the sixth sense door, which can be validly referred to as mind by the concept-term "mind". There is also not "objects out there, mind in here, and experience somewhere in-between". There is a third thing called "awareness" which exists being aware of the contents of mind and what mind cognizes. There are five senses (arising of mere experience: shapes, colors, the components of smell, components of taste, components of sound, components of touch) and mind as the sixth institution; this means, expressly, that there can be a third thing called "awareness" and a third thing called "experiencer who is aware of the experience". This awareness is deeply related to "no-self" because it does not judge the experience with craving or aversion.
</p><p>Clearly, the experience arises and is known by mind, but there is a third thing calls <a href="/wiki/Sati_(Buddhism)" title="Sati (Buddhism)">Sati</a> what is the "real experiencer of the experience" that sits apart from the experience and which can be aware of the experience in 4 levels. (Maha Sathipatthana Sutta.)
</p>
<ol><li>Body</li>
<li>Sensations (Changes of the body mind.)</li>
<li>Mind,</li>
<li>Contents of the mind. (Changes of the body mind.)</li></ol>
<p>To be aware of these four levels one needs to cultivate equanimity toward Craving and Aversion. This is Called Vipassana which is different from the way of reacting with  Craving and Aversion. This is the state of being aware and equanimous to the complete experience of here and now. This is the way of Buddhism, with regards to mind and the ultimate nature of minds (and persons).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mortality">Mortality</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mind&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Mortality">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Consciousness_after_death" title="Consciousness after death">Consciousness after death</a></div>
<p>Due to the <a href="/wiki/Mind%E2%80%93body_problem" title="Mind–body problem">mind–body problem</a>, a lot of interest and debate surrounds the question of what happens to one's conscious mind as one's body dies. During <a href="/wiki/Brain_death" title="Brain death">brain death</a> all <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brain_activity" title="Brain activity">brain function</a> permanently ceases. According to some neuroscientific views which see these processes as the physical basis of mental phenomena, the mind fails to survive brain death and ceases to exist. This permanent loss of consciousness after death is sometimes called "<a href="/wiki/Eternal_oblivion" title="Eternal oblivion">eternal oblivion</a>". The belief that some spiritual or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Incorporeal" title="Incorporeal">incorporeal</a> component (<a href="/wiki/Soul" title="Soul">soul</a>) exists and that it is preserved after death is described by the term "<a href="/wiki/Afterlife" title="Afterlife">afterlife</a>".
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Parapsychology">Parapsychology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mind&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Parapsychology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Parapsychology" title="Parapsychology">Parapsychology</a> is the study of certain types of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paranormal_phenomena" title="Paranormal phenomena">paranormal phenomena</a>, or of phenomena which appear to be paranormal or not have any scientific basis,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> such as <a href="/wiki/Precognition" title="Precognition">precognition</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Telekinesis" title="Telekinesis">telekinesis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Telepathy" title="Telepathy">telepathy</a>.
</p><p>The term is based on the Greek <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/para-" title="wikt:para-"><i>para</i></a> ('beside, beyond'), <a href="/wiki/Psyche_(psychology)" title="Psyche (psychology)"><i>psyche</i></a> ('soul, mind'), and <i><a href="/wiki/Logos" title="Logos">logos</a></i> ('account, explanation') and was coined by psychologist <a href="/wiki/Max_Dessoir" title="Max Dessoir">Max Dessoir</a> in or before 1889.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EncyOccult_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-EncyOccult-130">[130]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/J.B._Rhine" title="J.B. Rhine">J.B. Rhine</a> tried to popularize "parapsychology" using fraudulent techniques as a replacement for the earlier term "psychical research", during a shift in methodologies which brought experimental methods to the study of psychic phenomena.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EncyOccult_130-1"><a href="#cite_note-EncyOccult-130">[130]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Parapsychology" title="Parapsychology">Parapsychology</a> is not accepted among the scientific community as science, as <a href="/wiki/Psychic" title="Psychic">psychic</a> abilities have not been demonstrated to exist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CaliBoard_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-CaliBoard-131">[131]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NAS_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-NAS-134">[134]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNNSweden_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-CNNSweden-135">[135]</a></sup> The status of parapsychology as a <a href="/wiki/Science" title="Science">science</a> has also been disputed,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> with many scientists regarding the discipline as <a href="/wiki/Pseudoscience" title="Pseudoscience">pseudoscience</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cordón_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cordón-137">[137]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mind&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist">

<li id="cite_note-Cordón-137"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Cordón_137-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFCordón,_Luis_A.2005">Cordón, Luis A. (2005). <a class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/popularpsycholog0000cord/page/182" rel="nofollow"><i>Popular psychology: an encyclopedia</i></a>. Westport, Conn: <a href="/wiki/Greenwood_Publishing_Group" title="Greenwood Publishing Group">Greenwood Press</a>. p. <a class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/popularpsycholog0000cord/page/182" rel="nofollow">182</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-313-32457-4" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-313-32457-4"><bdi>978-0-313-32457-4</bdi></a>. <q>The essential problem is that a large portion of the scientific community, including most research psychologists, regards parapsychology as a pseudoscience, due largely to its failure to move beyond null results in the way science usually does. Ordinarily, when experimental evidence fails repeatedly to support a hypothesis, that hypothesis is abandoned. Within parapsychology, however, more than a century of experimentation has failed even to conclusively demonstrate the mere existence of paranormal phenomenon, yet parapsychologists continue to pursue that elusive goal.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Popular+psychology%3A+an+encyclopedia&amp;rft.place=Westport%2C+Conn&amp;rft.pages=182&amp;rft.pub=Greenwood+Press&amp;rft.date=2005&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-313-32457-4&amp;rft.au=Cord%C3%B3n%2C+Luis+A.&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Farchive.org%2Fdetails%2Fpopularpsycholog0000cord%2Fpage%2F182&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMind"></span></span>
